          <div class="Pos-r Z-0 article-container legacy" data-template="desktop" id="article-twin-peaks-showtime-exec-producer-mark-frost-talks-160003476" style="background-color:white;min-height:315px;">
           <div class="Pos-r sticky-container print-article" style="min-height:315px;">
            <div class="article-inner-container" style="max-width:1280px;">
             <div class="inset-container Mx-a">
              <div class="GridTable">
               <div class="D-tbr row-template">
                <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left">
                 <div class="content" style="width:825px;min-width:825px;">
                  <noscript>
                  </noscript>
                  <noscript>
                  </noscript>
                  <div class="GridTable grid-content">
                   <div class="D-tbr row-content">
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-left Pend-20" style="width:305px;max-width:305px;">
                     <h1 class="Font-A-6-110 title W-100" id="article-aft-title-twin-peaks-showtime-exec-producer-mark-frost-talks-160003476">
                      Twin Peaks on Showtime: Exec Producer Mark Frost Talks Returning Cast, Storyline and (Much) More
                     </h1>
                     <div class="attribution-component D-b W-100" id="article-aft-attribution-twin-peaks-showtime-exec-producer-mark-frost-talks-160003476" style="max-width:305px;">
                      <div class="author-info author-info-text-first Pt-10 W-100 Bd-t Bd-b Bdstart-0 Bdend-0">
                       <div class="GridTable W-100">
                        <div class="D-tbr">
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t provider-info">
                          <a class="provider-logo" href="http://www.tvline.com" target="_blank">
                           <img alt="TVLine.com" class="Maw-100" src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/FaHXaJZ715ZF0FsgY_ljNg--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO2ZpPWZpdDt3PTE1MA--/https://s.yimg.com/os/publish-images/tv/2014-12-10/ec8191e0-7fff-11e4-8aed-a1f0aad1262c_Screen-Shot-2014-12-09-at-4-01-45-PM.png"/>
                          </a>
                          <div class="provider-alias C-n">
                           <a class="Font-C-2-140 Fw-b" href="http://www.tvline.com" target="_blank">
                            TVLine.com
                           </a>
                          </div>
                         </div>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                       <div class="GridTable W-100">
                        <div class="D-tbr">
                         <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t">
                          <cite class="byline col D-b Fs-n" style="padding-bottom:15px;">
                           <span class="Font-C-2-140 Fw-n D-b">
                            Michael Ausiello
                           </span>
                           <time class="date Font-C-2-140 Fw-n D-b">
                            <span>
                             October 6, 2014
                            </span>
                           </time>
                          </cite>
                         </div>
                        </div>
                       </div>
                      </div>
                     </div>
                    </div>
                    <div class="GridTable-Cell Va-t col-right" style="max-width:500px;">
                     <div class="text-body-wrapper W-100 Font-B-1-160">
                      <noscript>
                      </noscript>
                      <div class="text-body W-100 Font-B-1-160" id="article-aft-text-body-twin-peaks-showtime-exec-producer-mark-frost-talks-160003476" style="color:#222222;max-width:500px;">
                       <div class="body read-more-cut">
                        <div class="pre-cut" style="height:auto;margin-bottom:1.5em;">
                         <p>
                          In the series finale of
                          <em>
                           Twin Peaks
                          </em>
                          , the late Laura Palmer looked into Agent Coopers eyes in the infamous Red Room and promised, Ill see you again in 25 years.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Girlfriends keeping her promise!
                          <span id="more-553313">
                          </span>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Earlier today, Showtime announcedthat it had ordered a
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:7a73e759-d518-3370-b8f3-c9e05b0df4f5;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://tvline.com/2014/10/06/twin-peaks-showtime-season-3-air-date-2016/" target="_blank">
                           nine-episode continuation of David Lynch and Mark Frosts seminal drama series
                          </a>
                          , to debut in 2016  AKA the 25th anniversary of that fateful episode.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          Were the seeds for this revival really planted back in 1991? Thats just one of the burning questions Frost tackles in the following Q&amp;A.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           PHOTOS
                          </strong>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:7a73e759-d518-3370-b8f3-c9e05b0df4f5;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://tvline.com/gallery/twin-peaks-showtime-cast-returning-season-3-kyle-maclachlan/#!1/tp14/" target="_blank">
                           <em>
                            Twin Peaks
                           </em>
                           on Showtime: 15 Original Characters That Must Be Brought Back
                          </a>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           TVLINE | For about two years now, rumors have been circulating about a
                           <em>
                            Twin Peaks
                           </em>
                           revival being in the works. How long have you and David been formulating this?
                          </strong>
                          <br/>
                          David and I stayed in touch and remained closed friends throughout all these years. It was about three years ago this summer we were having lunch at [famed Hollywood eatery] Musso &amp; Frank, where we often used to go. And we were just kicking stuff around and we started getting some ideas in our heads about
                          <em>
                           Twin Peaks
                          </em>
                          . Suddenly, it felt like a place we wanted to visit again. And that was the kickoff.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           TVLINE | Was Showtime the first place you went?
                          </strong>
                          <br/>
                          We didnt go to anybody else. Showtime was the first and only [network] we spoke to about this. There was a nice sense of continuity there, because Gary Levine, whos the right-hand man to [Showtime president] David Nevins, was our [creative] representative on the show when we were on ABC. Weve known Gary a long time. We trust Gary. We like Gary. We had a really great meeting with them. And David [Lynch] really loved the artwork on David [Nevins] office walls. And they loved the show. And thats how it all came to be.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           TVLINE | Just to confirm, this is
                           <em>
                            not
                           </em>
                           a remake, correct? Its a continuation, like TNTs
                           <em>
                            Dallas
                           </em>
                           ?
                          </strong>
                          <br/>
                          It is not a remake. The story continues. The seeds of where we go were planted where weve been.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           TVLINE | In the series finale, Laura Palmer tells Agent Cooper in the Red Room, Ill see you again in 25 years. That cant be a coincidence, can it?
                          </strong>
                          <br/>
                          When you see it, youll know.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <img alt="Twin Peaks on Showtime: Exec Producer Mark Frost Talks Returning Cast, Storyline and (Much) More" class="aligncenter size-full wp-image-553316" height="357" src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/NRC80ry65fyW7xQUwdkDCQ--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9ODAw/http://pmctvline2.files.wordpress.com/2014/10/25.jpg?w=550&amp;h=357" width="800"/>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           TVLINE | Are you looking at this as Season 3 of
                           <em>
                            Twin Peaks
                           </em>
                           ?
                          </strong>
                          <br/>
                          Not really, but just because my brain doesnt work that way. Ive always said that
                          <em>
                           Twin Peaks
                          </em>
                          to me was like a novel we filmed every page of. So this is more like we found another volume of the saga, and now we want to bring that to life too.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           TVLINE | Will the nine episodes revolve around a new mystery?
                          </strong>
                          <br/>
                          If I told you that I would have to give the Kill command to the Predator drones that are circling your house now. And that wouldnt be cool. [
                          <em>
                           Laughs
                          </em>
                          ]
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           TVLINE | Will the world of
                           <em>
                            Fire Walk With Me
                           </em>
                           be considered a part of the Canon?
                          </strong>
                          <br/>
                          I think it should be. Its definitely part of the mythology of the show, and it reflects the work that was done before and it will have some bearing on the work as we go forward.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           TVLINE | Is it your goal to bring back as many of the original cast as possible?
                          </strong>
                          <br/>
                          Those who want to see old faces, and those would like to see new faces, none of them will be disappointed. Its far too early to talk specifics about people. Were not at that stage in the process.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           <img alt="Bob" class="alignright size-full wp-image-553345" data-src="https://s.yimg.com/lo/api/res/1.2/rOul0OsTPlzReZmbRdg7jA--/YXBwaWQ9bWFnYXppbmVzO3c9ODAw/http://pmctvline2.files.wordpress.com/2014/10/bob.jpg?w=240&amp;h=184" height="184" src="https://s.yimg.com/g/images/spaceball.gif" width="800"/>
                           TVLINE | In the past 25 years, several cast members have passed away, most notably former set dresser turned scariest TV character ever, Frank Silva (AKA Killer Bob). How will you handle that loss?
                          </strong>
                          <br/>
                          I cant really say. Thats a tough one to go into without giving away too much.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           TVLINE | In his book Reflections:
                           <em>
                            An Oral History of Twin Peaks
                           </em>
                           , journalist Brad Dukes explored some of the issues that may have compromised the storytelling of Season 2 and the longevity of the show. There was a lot of pressure from ABC to wrap up the murder, and both you and David were being pulled away by other projects. With both of you fully on board and committed to these nine episodes, would you say that show might lean back towards the heights of Season 1?
                          </strong>
                          <br/>
                          That would certainly be our goal and intention We decided at that first lunch that if we were going to do this it had to be the two of us. It started with us and we felt it was only right if it continued with the two of us. So we pledged right then and there that we were going to write it ourselves, and David said he wanted to direct all of them. And well produce them together. Thats the basis on which we decided to go forward.
                         </p>
                        </div>
                        <div class="post-cut W-100" id="post-cut" style="transition-property:none;-webkit-transition-property:none;transition-duration:10s;-webkit-transition-duration:10s;transition-timing-function:ease-in;-webkit-transition-timing-function:ease-in;overflow:hidden;max-height:0;max-width:500px;">
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           RELATED
                          </strong>
                          <a data-ylk="elm:itm;elmt:link;t1:a2;t2:article;t3:body;t8:7a73e759-d518-3370-b8f3-c9e05b0df4f5;t9:18;itc:0" href="http://tvline.com/2014/10/06/twin-peaks-spoilers-season-3-evil-agent-cooper/" target="_blank">
                           <em>
                            Twin Peaks
                           </em>
                           Is Back: 14 Burning Questions Season 3 Must Address
                          </a>
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           TVLINE Will the new series be a Valentine to hardcore fans, or are you setting out to bring in a new generation of acolytes?
                          </strong>
                          <br/>
                          Its fair to say that there arent many shows that have a fan base as passionate and dedicated and committed as our show does. And were very grateful to those people for keeping the flames alive all these years, and helping whole new generations of people discover it. So, in a way, this will be of special significance to those folks. And at the same time we hope a whole bunch of people want to come to the party as well.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           TVLINE | Will Angelo Badalamentido the score?
                          </strong>
                          <br/>
                          Too early to say.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           TVLINE | The TV climate is very different than when
                           <em>
                            Twin Peaks
                           </em>
                           debuted 25 years ago. There was nothing else like it at the time. Since then, the show has inspired dozens  if not hundreds  of imitators. Any concern that the novelty has worn off?
                          </strong>
                          <br/>
                          Well, the novelty hasnt worn off for
                          <em>
                           us
                          </em>
                          . I think well be able to effectively translate that into todays cultural language without too much trouble.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           TVLINE | If its a success, could there be more?
                          </strong>
                          <br/>
                          Weve learned never to say never. Anything is a possibility.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           TVLINE | What does it mean personally to you to revisit this material 25 years later?
                          </strong>
                          <br/>
                          I think for me, and for everybody who took part in this originally, it was  its a terrible pun  a peak experience. And the chance to revisit it later in life, and see what we can do now that we didnt know then, is a once-in-a-lifetime opportunity.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           TVLINE | The second season was rather polarizing, and some fans felt let down by how the story ended. Are you looking at this as an opportunity to bring the story to a more satisfying conclusion?
                          </strong>
                          <br/>
                          Its our hope that these episodes will give the fans everything they felt they hadnt gotten the last time we left off.
                         </p>
                         <p>
                          <strong>
                           TVLINE | Lastly, Id be remiss if I didnt ask, hows Annie?
                          </strong>
                          <br/>
                          [
                          <em>
                           Laughs
                          </em>
                          ] Funnily enough, I just showed the second
                          <em>
                           Austin Powers
                          </em>
                          movie to my son last night, who asked me about [Heather Graham]. And I said, Oh, thats Annie. And he said, Whos Annie? And I said, No, no. The question is
                          <em>
                           Hows
                          </em>
                          Annie? And judging by how Annie looked in that movie Id say Annies fine.
                         </p>
                         <div>

root.App.Cache.genUrl = function (routeName, context) {
        var route = routeMap[routeName],
            path, keys, i, len, key, param, regex;

        if (!route) { return ''; }

        path = route.path;
        keys = route.keys;

        if (context &amp;&amp; (len = keys.length)) {
            for (i = 0; i &lt; len; i += 1) {
                key   = keys[i];
                param = key.name || key;
                regex = new RegExp('[:*]' + param + '\\b');
                path  = path.replace(regex, context[param]);
            }
        }

        // Replace missing params with empty strings.
        return path.replace(/([:*])([\w\-]+)?/g, '');
    };

It was about three years ago this summer we were having lunch at [famed Hollywood eatery] Musso &amp; Frank, where we often used to go. And we were just kicking stuff around and we started getting some ideas in our heads about \u003Cem\u003ETwin Peaks\u003C\u002Fem\u003E. Suddenly, it felt like a place we wanted to visit again. Showtime was the first and only [network] we spoke to about this. There was a nice sense of continuity there, because Gary Levine, who&#x2019;s the right-hand man to [Showtime president] David Nevins, was our [creative] representative on the show when we were on ABC. We&#x2019;ve known Gary a long time. We trust Gary. We like Gary. We had a really great meeting with them. And David [Lynch] really loved the artwork on David [Nevins]&#x2018; office walls. There was a lot of pressure from ABC to wrap up the murder, and both you and David were being pulled away by other projects. With both of you fully on board and committed to these nine episodes, would you say that show might lean back towards the heights of Season 1?\u003C\u002Fstrong\u003E\u003Cbr\u003E That would certainly be our goal and intention&#x2026; We decided at that first lunch that if we were going to do this it had to be the two of us.
